  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

  <span id="freeText4029655142269475695" style="display:none"><i>An alternative cover edition for this ISBN can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45692416" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i><br /><br />Rachel catches the same commuter train every morning. She knows it will wait at the same signal each time, overlooking a row of back gardens. She’s even started to feel like she knows the people who live in one of the houses. “Jess and Jason,” she calls them. Their life—as she sees it—is perfect. If only Rachel could be that happy. And then she sees something shocking. It’s only a minute until the train moves on, but it’s enough. Now everything’s changed. Now Rachel has a chance to become a part of the lives she’s only watched from afar. Now they’ll see; she’s much more than just the girl on the train...</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/302728-if-i-hated-gone-girl-am-i-going-to-hate">If I hated &quot;Gone Girl&quot; am I going to hate &quot;The Girl on the Train&quot;? Obviously not looking for someone with a crystal ball, just informed (like you&#39;ve read both books and &quot;they&#39;re not really that much alike&quot;) opinions.</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1528390751i/4622890._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Having read both, I would say probably not. Though I agree with the person who said "it depends why you hated Gone Girl". I thought Gone Girl was too <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Having read both, I would say probably not. Though I agree with the person who said "it depends why you hated Gone Girl". I thought Gone Girl was too slow, especially in the first half, but I liked the grittiness. The Girl on the Train was fast-paced and creepier (in a good way, if you ask me). It took me a week to read Gone Girl and I read The Girl on the Train in a single sitting. <br /><br />Similarities with Gone Girl: immoral/unconventional female narrators, psychological thriller, unreliable narrators, dark and gritty.<br /><br />Differences: Faster-paced, more traditional mystery, more gripping (in my opinion), a very different kind of ending.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I had to force myself to continue reading this book, so it took longer than usual. I would not, not not, compare it to Gone Girl in any way. Gone Girl<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I had to force myself to continue reading this book, so it took longer than usual. I would not, not not, compare it to Gone Girl in any way. Gone Girl was a good novel and well written. Disliked all of the characters in Girl on the Train immensely. Cannot understand why all the hype about this book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1065186199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065186199" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065186199?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780857522313" href="/book/show/21840310-the-girl-on-the-train">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065186199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13131142835339198343"><i>I once read a book by a former alcoholic where she described giving oral sex to two different men, men she'd just met in a restaurant on a busy London high street. I read it and I thought, I'm not <b>that</b> bad. This is where the bar is set.</i><br/><br/>oh, yeah - this one is going to be a must-read for those people looking to find their next <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a> experience. it's an incredibly fast-paced and engrossing psychological thriller, and i was on board as soon as i read the editor's bit of ARC-copy, even though i k</span>
  <span id="freeText13131142835339198343" style="display:none"><i>I once read a book by a former alcoholic where she described giving oral sex to two different men, men she'd just met in a restaurant on a busy London high street. I read it and I thought, I'm not <b>that</b> bad. This is where the bar is set.</i><br><br>oh, yeah - this one is going to be a must-read for those people looking to find their next <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> experience. it's an incredibly fast-paced and engrossing psychological thriller, and i was on board as soon as i read the editor's bit of ARC-copy, even though i know that writing those things is part of the job and not at all unbiased. but it's hard not to be swayed when you read:<br><br><i>Within days of my introducing the manuscript in March, people from every department were regularly pulling me aside to testify to how much they loved the read, how they couldn't put it down. At a recent meeting, a colleague who was twelve pages from the end was secretly reading them under the table because she could not stop. Another had the manuscript propped up next to her phone so she could read between calls, and last week in the elevator, people around me suddenly started competing over who'd read it fastest, and who was more surprised by the ending. You know you have something special when it becomes watercooler talk for months on end.</i><br><br>it would take a very stubbornly cynical person to see that as anything other than genuine enthusiasm. <br><br>and the book definitely delivers. it is an absolute page-turner with a number of unreliable narrators ranging from the self-deluded to the spotty memory of the blackout drunk. <br><br>i am too busy reading on my daily commute to notice my fellow passengers unless they are smelly/behaving in an unstable manner (frequently), or exceptionally attractive (MUCH less frequently), but apparently this is a thing that commuters do - notice their fellow travelers, making up stories about their lives, speculating about what they do when they're not in the in-between moments of their day. and rachel does it more than most. rachel is blisteringly lonely, drowning the sorrows of her failed marriage with grim determination and canned gin and tonics and endless bottles of wine. she has lost her job because of her perpetual drunkenness, but rather than tell her flatmate, she keeps taking the train into london every day, pretending to go to work, but actually just getting drunk in various places, and happily fantasizing about the young couple she watches every day from her train window; a couple who live a few doors down from her old house, where her ex-husband tom still resides with his new wife and baby girl. <br><br>still reeling from tom's infidelity to her, she nonetheless would love to be back with him, and in this golden couple she observes and imagines, calling them "jess and jason," she sees the life she could have had with tom. one day, while commuting/gazing voyeuristically, she witnesses "jess" on her front lawn with another man, in what appears to be a romantic clinch. she is outraged at this display, as personally offended as if the infidelity were being committed against herself. shortly after this episode, she learns that "jess," actually named megan, has disappeared, and feeling connected to this couple she has never actually met, she insinuates herself into the investigation, meeting with both the police and megan's husband, actual name scott. <br><br>the story is told from three perspectives: rachel's, megan's, and tom's new wife anna, and covers all the traditional viewpoints of the typical domestic drama: the jilted lover, the other woman, the cheating wife. all three of these women are simultaneously sympathetic and repellent, which is tricky to pull off. and as for the mystery of megan's disappearance itself, well that path splits and splits again in a wonderful head-spinning journey where not a single character avoids suspicion (except MAYBE tom and anna's infant daughter); i think there are seven characters in total who appear to be the culprit at one point or another, and each seems as plausible as the next. it is a fantastic ride, and hawkins does a great job with both the mystery elements and the character development, with great attention to detail, and fully established backstories and motivations. even when you cringe at some of the choices, they completely make sense for the character. it is a lot of fun, and terribly addictive. much better than a meeting, i kid you not.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13131142835339198343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1167297695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167297695" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167297695?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=addiction">addiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167297695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7316584449686445492">“Esssscuse me. Is this seat taken? Thanks. I like to sits bys the wimdow. Would you likes a little bit of wine? You know what they say, a little vino would be keen-o. No? Mores for me then. Oh, check it out. *BURP* WhatwasIsaying? Oh, sees that house over there going by? That used to be my house. True story. Me and my husbadand lived there. But the ole bastard cheated on me and lefts me and then he marriesss that stupid cow and then he knockeded her up and now they got a stupid cow kid and they </span>
  <span id="freeText7316584449686445492" style="display:none">“Esssscuse me. Is this seat taken? Thanks. I like to sits bys the wimdow. Would you likes a little bit of wine? You know what they say, a little vino would be keen-o. No? Mores for me then. Oh, check it out. *BURP* WhatwasIsaying? Oh, sees that house over there going by? That used to be my house. True story. Me and my husbadand lived there. But the ole bastard cheated on me and lefts me and then he marriesss that stupid cow and then he knockeded her up and now they got a stupid cow kid and they lives in my house! Can you believes that? I means, it’s not my house now, but it usesed to be. Now he the rottens old bastard lives there with his stupids new wife and their stupid battery….Did I say battery? I meant baby. I’ve hads a few gin &amp; tonics...And a little wine...*BURP*<br /><br />Anyhows, letsus not talk about my stupid ole ex-husband. See that other house? The ones just a couple a few doors downs from my old one where you can totallys see their deck? A beausfiful couple lives there. They’re just the bestus. They’s just gorgeous and you can tells that they are for sure in loves 100%. You’d never catch *BURP* that guy cheatins on her, I can promise you that! I watch them every time I goes by on this here trainy-train with my glasses of wine as I ride, and I can just tell that their greatests most happiest couple who ever was…Lots better than the my stupid ole ex. Seeing them be such a absofantabulous couple rights by where I used to live is the one part of my stupid day I enjoy when I ride this train.<br /> <br />Wass that you say? She’s missing? Been in all the papers? Thattsus just terriblez… Geez, I can’t imagine how I *BURP* missed that news…. Since Saturday, you says? … I think I was down there last Saturday..Thass right. I remembers now. I had a couple of drinkies and went to sees my ole husband to tells him that I still love ‘em….Err.. I mean that I hate ‘em.. Thass right. I hate ‘em! But I had ones or twos too many, and I blacked out…. And I had a cut on my head the next day and a feeling that I’d seen something terribles…. Do ya think maybes I saw something? I better go *BURP* tell the cops about this….But first Imma gonna puke all over your shoes. Sorry about this……..”<br /><br />*****<br /><br />That’s what this book feels like, that you got stuck sitting next to a sloppy drunk who is telling you this story, and maybe you feel a little bad for her even as you’re trying to avoid her spilling her drink on you. After listening to her inebriated babblings for a very short while you immediately know more about her situation than she does, and you could easily tell her what she missed. But then you catch a whiff of her breath so you just try to sneak away when she’s not paying attention. Seriously, I might have liked this more if I hadn’t figured out who the culprit was about three minutes into the book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1066690960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1066690960" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066690960?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780857522313" href="/book/show/21840310-the-girl-on-the-train">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066690960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7631008656113877226"><blockquote>
  <b>"Something bad happened."</b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Are you ready for a faster-paced, creepier <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a>?</i><br/><br/>Woah. This is one unsettling little thriller and the best bit about it is that <b>no one can be trusted</b>, including the three female narrators who share the storytelling of this book. I literally read this entire novel in one sitting and I now need to find the words to convince you to go get your hands on it. RIGHT NOW.<br/><br/>Between an alcoholic, a liar and a cheat, <b>who can you trust?</b> These are the three women at the centre </span>
  <span id="freeText7631008656113877226" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"Something bad happened."</b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Are you ready for a faster-paced, creepier <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>?</i><br /><br />Woah. This is one unsettling little thriller and the best bit about it is that <b>no one can be trusted</b>, including the three female narrators who share the storytelling of this book. I literally read this entire novel in one sitting and I now need to find the words to convince you to go get your hands on it. RIGHT NOW.<br /><br />Between an alcoholic, a liar and a cheat, <b>who can you trust?</b> These are the three women at the centre of this book: Rachel, Anna and Megan. <br /><br />Have you ever sat on the train, glanced at the people around you or out of the window, and made up stories about them? Maybe you've even gone so far as to invent names for these people and imagine their perfect or not-so-perfect lives. <br /><br />Rachel is that girl on the train who takes her mind off her own life by imagining the lives of others. Specifically the lives of "Jess and Jason" who live at the house outside her train window when the train stops at the same red signal every morning. But then one morning, things are not as they are supposed to be and Rachel sees something that completely shatters the "Jess and Jason" image which exists in her head.<br /><br />Now she is pulled into their lives. Unsure exactly what she knows but certain she cannot rest until she finds out. <br /><br /><b>This book is just full of secrets.</b> Everyone has them. It's about all the little mysteries that exist just outside of what we see on the surface. What goes on behind closed doors? How much can you ever really know a person? What horrors exist in that black spot of your memory from Saturday night?<br /><br /><b>It was fascinating, gripping and oh so very creepy.</b> Hawkins has been added to the small group of thriller authors on my "must buy" list.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7631008656113877226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13639656374245424177">I just sent a 3 page, 3,000 word email about why I didn't like this book to a friend, and I still feel the urge to express myself. I suppose that tells you just how much I disliked it.<br/><br/>This thing is a hot mess, the writing is clumsy, there are things that don't make any sense, the characters are pathetic and the opposite of complex. The women in this book are either defined by the men they are dating/married to, or by how they feel about being a mother (and by that I mean, do they already have a </span>
  <span id="freeText13639656374245424177" style="display:none">I just sent a 3 page, 3,000 word email about why I didn't like this book to a friend, and I still feel the urge to express myself. I suppose that tells you just how much I disliked it.<br /><br />This thing is a hot mess, the writing is clumsy, there are things that don't make any sense, the characters are pathetic and the opposite of complex. The women in this book are either defined by the men they are dating/married to, or by how they feel about being a mother (and by that I mean, do they already have a child, do they want a child, or <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[does their character arc end with getting excited about being pregnant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>?) Bleugh. The 'plot twist' is easy to guess not even halfway through the book, and the who-dun-it moment, where we find out who the bad guy is, while predictable, doesn't make any sense to me, considered how this book is written and what we know about the characters. Exposition, people. There isn't any. You might argue that it's because of the unreliable narrator, but I'm not buying it. Good writing works its way around it. Also, I didn't know 'thriller' translated to 'no character development'. <br /><br />And have I mentioned the clumsy writing? Because I was getting secondhand embarrassment 85% of the time. This book was, above all things (that I honestly didn't care about), awkward.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1158639511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2797203199839648127"><b>4.5 stars</b> Everyone in this book is absolutely <i>terrible</i>, and as a result, this book is a masterpiece in character study and development. It's also a well-written, precisely plotted psychological thriller, and deftly sketches one unreliable narrator after another. I guessed the culprit not too far into the book, but that didn't spoil my reading experience at all, particularly because the author drops so many diverting and convincing red herrings into the story. <br/><br/>I think it's also interesting that t</span>
  <span id="freeText2797203199839648127" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> Everyone in this book is absolutely <i>terrible</i>, and as a result, this book is a masterpiece in character study and development. It's also a well-written, precisely plotted psychological thriller, and deftly sketches one unreliable narrator after another. I guessed the culprit not too far into the book, but that didn't spoil my reading experience at all, particularly because the author drops so many diverting and convincing red herrings into the story. <br /><br />I think it's also interesting that the central character, Rachel, challenges readers to think about how much we assume about--and pre-judge--other people based on our limited knowledge of them. To feel pity, disgust, frustration, compassion, and so much more for one character is a rare thing. <br /><br />Recommended to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9736930.Before_I_Go_To_Sleep" title="Before I Go To Sleep by S.J. Watson" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Go To Sleep</a>, and for YA readers, fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16074758.Dangerous_Girls" title="Dangerous Girls by Abigail Haas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Girls</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2741432.Nova_Ren_Suma" title="Nova Ren Suma" rel="nofollow noopener">Nova Ren Suma</a>. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166914631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4087164527870217151">What a huge disappointment. <br/>The concept sounded amazing, and it got off to a promising...if slow...start. But it quickly turned into this messy, melodramatic story that was neither surprising, or original. Much like in Gone Girl, there was not a single likable character in the entire book. That wasn't the main problem for me, though. I could see the ending coming from a mile away. Actually more like I figured out who the main villan was within the first 20 pages. Never a ringing endorsement. <br/></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1296579887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296579887" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296579887?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296579887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer795541196180356312">I read this one out of curiosity. Aware that it had been a huge market success, I wondered if it merited the sales. According to Riverhead, <i>The Girl on the Train</i> is, or was, the fastest-selling adult hardcover fiction debut ever. And that is a shame. With so many great books being published every year that do little or no business, for this one to have secured a first class ticket on the book-sales express can only be dispiriting to the good and great writers everywhere toiling away in third cla</span>
  <span id="freeText795541196180356312" style="display:none">I read this one out of curiosity. Aware that it had been a huge market success, I wondered if it merited the sales. According to Riverhead, <i>The Girl on the Train</i> is, or was, the fastest-selling adult hardcover fiction debut ever. And that is a shame. With so many great books being published every year that do little or no business, for this one to have secured a first class ticket on the book-sales express can only be dispiriting to the good and great writers everywhere toiling away in third class on the oft-delayed local.<br><br>I do not mean to say that <i>The Girl…</i> is a bad book. Although I believe it to be seriously flawed, it is most definitely entertaining and will no doubt help hundreds of thousands of readers while away a few hours of their (our) lives, getting from this station to that. But if you want a psychological thriller that doesn’t disregard red signals you would do better to book a seat elsewhere.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436524934i/15471846._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Paula Hawkins</b><br><br>Rachel Watson has had a tough go of it. When her hopes of having a baby with hubby Tom did not work out, she landed in a trough of post-hope depression, and self-medicated with a steady flow of what seemed happier spirits. It did not work out. Now, divorced and unemployed as a result of her drinking, growing larger and pastier by the day, Rachel rides the commuter train to London on weekday mornings, pretending she is still working, pretending she still has a life. The ride takes her past her old neighborhood, offering a nice, mood dampening view of a stretch of railroad-edge homes. She used to live in one of those, before her ex bought out her interest. A few places away from her former home there is a couple she sees most days. She imagines lives for them, nursing this fantasy for quite some time, until she learns that the woman has vanished, and the game is afoot.<br><br>The notion for the story occurred to Hawkins on her regular train ride in London some years back. She calls it “Rear-Window-ish,” noting that it is hardly unusual for train riders to be curious about the lives being lived in the houses they pass, and just as likely for those on the ground to wonder about those passing by. <blockquote>
<b> I used to go to college on the District line,” she said. “It goes very, very slowly and you can look into people’s houses. I did idly wonder about what you would do if you saw an act of violence or something suspicious. It’s quite normal, everyone is curious about other people’s lives.” </b> - from an article in the Standard</blockquote>This irregular Watson will not make anyone forget the investigative Doctor, let alone his illustrious partner, but Rachel feels compelled to find out whatever she can, using the knowledge she has gleaned from her daily observations. We expect our investigators these days to be a bit down on their luck, and to throw back maybe more than their share of amber liquid. But Rachel Watson doesn’t have a drinking problem, she has a drinking catastrophe. How is she to figure out whither the missing lady has gone, or perhaps who made her go missing, how is she to judge whether the lady’s anger-management-challenged husband, the other man she saw at her place, or someone else might be somehow involved, if her drinking causes her to have more blackouts than London during the blitz.<br><br>The tale is told in staggered chronology, from three perspectives. Rachel’s, the missing person’s, and Anna’s, she being the woman with whom Rachel’s ex cheated while he was still with Rachel, and whom he subsequently married. Or she said, she said, and then she said. The timelines converge at the end. Most sections are divided into sub headings of morning, evening, afternoon, that sort. It makes for many short passages, good, appropriately, for reading on a train.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436526505i/15472079._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b> This is an example of the S stock used on the District line Hawkins once rode</b><br><br>The pace of the tale is quick, clickety-clacking along without exceeding posted limits, advancing nicely to the big climax. Truthfulness comes in for some attention, as it seems everyone has something to hide. If you are looking for likeable characters, you might try the Hogwarts Express. The folks here tote enough baggage to merit their own cars. I suppose Rachel is sympathetic, but seems almost as much an agent of her misery as a victim. Making her pathetic and annoying was, I expect, a way to make her real, make her sympathetic, and that works, to a point. <br><br>Will Rachel find out what happened with the missing woman? Will her ex take out an order of protection against her, as she keeps calling and showing up at his place? Is the missing person merely missing? or worse? Can Rachel stay sober long enough to figure anything out? You might very well care. Clearly, judging by sales, many do. But, while I did, a little, I felt pushed away by this book. I felt cheated, as an actual audience member, as if riding on a disoriented express. I do understand that the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unreliable_narrator" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">unreliable narrator</a> is simply a story-telling mechanism and that Rachel falls into the <i>Madman</i> classification within that, but when she changes her story about a significant piece of information the story went off the rails for me. So, while there is plenty to enjoy about <i>The Girl on the Train</i>, while there is plenty of tension-release-repeat, and while many readers are bound to be transported by the story, relating to or rooting for one or more characters at least some of the time, the one thing a reader demands from an author is honesty, and when trust is lost so is the benefit of the several hours we spend together. The locomotive was transformed, for me, into a hand-car trapped in a siding. It’s elementary.<br><br>Review first posted – 7/10/15<br><br>Publication date – 1/13/15<br>Movie opened - 10/7/16<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>While this may be the first novel by <i>Paula Hawkins</i>, it is not the first novel that Paula Hawkins wrote, or published. She got work writing chick-lit under the name Amy Silver, an experience that she says was great training. Hawkins, born and raised in Zimbabwe, was 17 when her family moved to London. She had wanted to be a foreign correspondent like her father, but decided that war zones were just too scary. Check the Guardian piece if you are interested in getting more info on the author. <br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://paulahawkinsbooks.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/paulahwrites" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/amysilverwriter" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter as Amy Silver,</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/PaulaHawkinsWriter" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> pages<br><br>Excellent intel in this piece in <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015/apr/21/the-girl-on-the-train-paula-hawkins-new-gone-girl-female-thriller-authors-gillian-flynn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Guardian </a><br><br>Here is the article from the Standard cited in the review, <a href="http://www.standard.co.uk/news/london/my-district-line-commute-inspired-bestselling-thriller-says-london-author-paula-hawkins-10010185.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">'My District line commute inspired bestselling thriller,' says London author Paula Hawkins </a>,<br><br>An interview with the author in Entertainment Weekly <a href="http://www.standard.co.uk/news/london/my-district-line-commute-inspired-bestselling-thriller-says-london-author-paula-hawkins-10010185.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Girl on the Train author Paula Hawkins talks about her next thriller</a>, by Clark Collis<br><br>A few <i>great train reads</i>. Now don’t bug me about the brevity of this. I know there are only a gazillion. Do feel free, however to add your favorite train books in the comments. I will be happy to add those to this list if you like. I have not gotten around to installing links for all of these, but I expect you guys can manage<br><br><i>4.50 from Paddington</i> by Agatha Christie’s <br><i>Murder on the Orient Express</i> by AC<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/87282.Closely_Watched_Trains" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Closely Watched Trains</a> by Bohumil Hrabal, Edith Pargeter <br><i>The Great Train Robbery</i> by Michael Crichton<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/63690.The_Great_Railway_Bazaar" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Great Railway Bazaar </a> by Paul Theroux, or several other train books by this author <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24728470.M_Train" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">M Train</a> by Patti Smith - recommended by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7020601-mona" rel="nofollow noopener">Mona</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15677.Strangers_on_a_Train" rel="nofollow noopener"> Strangers on a Train </a> by Patricia Highsmith<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174093679" rel="nofollow noopener">A Train in Winter</a> by Caroline Moorehead - recommended for inclusion by Dianne<br><br>Not to be outdone, <b>TRAIN TUNES</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dlc6xCPx60U" rel="nofollow noopener">Can't You See</a> - recommended by Murf the Surf<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w8qTKyb0EcY" rel="nofollow noopener">Casey Jones</a> – this version by Allan Hirsch<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-XQybKMXL-k" rel="nofollow noopener"> Chatanooga Choo-Choo</a> – Glenn Miller Orchestra - recommended by Clif<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bDktBZzQIiU" rel="nofollow noopener"> Folsom Prison Blues (I hear that train a’comin)</a> – Johnny Cash<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sxP6BFMTW3M" rel="nofollow noopener">I’ve Been Working on the Railroad</a> – Pete Seeger<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZcXpKiY2MXE" rel="nofollow noopener">Last Train to Clarkesville</a> – The Monkees<br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-REw_YsBxto" rel="nofollow noopener">Last Train to Lhasa</a> -   <span id="freeText8489366348753892055" style="display:none">I tried to enjoy it! I swear I did! The hype told me that I had to! <br /><br />I wasn't bad, but it wasn't good either. <div id="review_1173568087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173568087" />
    <a title="Steffi ~mereadingbooks~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1065805-steffi-mereadingbooks"><img alt="Steffi ~mereadingbooks~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527708207p2/1065805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1173568087?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steffi ~mereadingbooks~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steffi ~mereadingbooks~" href="/user/show/1065805-steffi-mereadingbooks">Steffi ~mereadingbooks~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857522320" href="/book/show/23347055-the-girl-on-the-train">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1065805-steffi-mereadingbooks?shelf=crime-and-thriller">crime-and-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1065805-steffi-mereadingbooks?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1065805-steffi-mereadingbooks?shelf=hype">hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173568087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14262933289357829878">this review and more on my blog -> <a href='https://mereadingbooks.wordpress.com/2015/01/21/review-the-girl-on-the-train-by-paula-hawkins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>mereadingbooks</a><br/><br/><i>Caution. There might be some ranting ahead.</i><br/><br/>This has frequently been called the next <i>Gone Girl</i>. And yes, that is to some extend why I wanted to read this. I wanted something suspenseful; an unreliable narrator; and lots of “what the hell?!”- moments. Out of these three things I got one – an unreliable narrator. But one written so clumsily and shallow that I was annoyed, not intrigued, by her. <br/><br/>The plot’s mystery falls flat because it is done in such</span>
  <span id="freeText14262933289357829878" style="display:none">this review and more on my blog -&gt; <a href="https://mereadingbooks.wordpress.com/2015/01/21/review-the-girl-on-the-train-by-paula-hawkins/" rel="nofollow noopener">mereadingbooks</a><br /><br /><i>Caution. There might be some ranting ahead.</i><br /><br />This has frequently been called the next <i>Gone Girl</i>. And yes, that is to some extend why I wanted to read this. I wanted something suspenseful; an unreliable narrator; and lots of “what the hell?!”- moments. Out of these three things I got one – an unreliable narrator. But one written so clumsily and shallow that I was annoyed, not intrigued, by her. <br /><br />The plot’s mystery falls flat because it is done in such a heavy-handed way. The shift between narrative points of view and the two timelines seem like an artificial way of keeping the reader in the dark. The alcohol-induced blackouts of the main character just add to that feeling. I constantly thought “oh, how convenient that she does not remember that” and “oh, how convenient she can recall a tiny detail now”. It was simply clumsy and trite. <br /><br />However, the worst thing about Rachel, the protagonist and main narrator, weren’t the clichés about alcoholism and divorced women. These aspects annoyed me to no end but the absolute worst thing about Rachel and the two other female narrators was how pathetic they were. Throughout the book I got the feeling that Paula Hawkins must hate women; hate them with a passion. Women in this novel are portrayed as unstable (going on batshit crazy), weak, dependent (on men), and insecure. Every single woman mentioned defines her personality in relation to a man. They doubt themselves, their capabilities and decisions. The men, in contrast, are all mysterious but strong and sure of themselves. They are there to give definition and meaning to their wives, girlfriends, mistresses, and sons. Even those women on the side-lines of the plot are only defined by their relationships to men.<br /><br />For instance, Rachel’s mother; she is only mentioned two or three times and the one time she actually gets a few lines is when she explains how she’s not able to help her daughter at the moment because she has a new “friend” and she doesn’t want to scare him off like that! Seriously? Also, Rachel’s roommate is supposed to be the one thinking clearly; she tries to keep Rachel sober and wants her to go to AA meetings, get a grip on life, and so on. Still, even the supposedly reasonable character is defined by her boyfriend. When she’s not home she is with him and when he is out of town for some reason she sits at home waiting for him. And these are only the minor female characters in this novel.<br />Rachel, Anna, and Megan are all pathetic in their very own way. They pine about the men that leave or reject them; they doubt their life decisions and still won’t change anything in order not to upset their men. And every single thought they have is about how their decisions or actions might affect their husbands, ex-husbands, boyfriends, or lovers. <br /><br />I know I’m ranting a bit here, but this really really annoyed me. I also know what Hawkins was trying to do. She wanted to show the dark side of domestic life – just like <i>Gone Girl</i> did. But in my opinion she has utterly failed to do so.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14262933289357829878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1139207580&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139207580" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12482458995630751869">I am so disappointed in this one. It started out promising enough, but the writing and the drama got old fast. There was really only one person who could have done it, and because of that I kept thinking it must be someone else. But it wasn't someone else. It was THAT PERSON. By the time the big reveal happened, I was so ready for the whole thing to just be over already. I started out thinking I had a 4 star book in my hands. Halfway through I was looking for an excuse to give it 3 stars. Finall</span>
  <span id="freeText12482458995630751869" style="display:none">I am so disappointed in this one. It started out promising enough, but the writing and the drama got old fast. There was really only one person who could have done it, and because of that I kept thinking it must be someone else. But it wasn't someone else. It was THAT PERSON. By the time the big reveal happened, I was so ready for the whole thing to just be over already. I started out thinking I had a 4 star book in my hands. Halfway through I was looking for an excuse to give it 3 stars. Finally, with about 30 pages left, I knew that 2 stars was going to be a gift. Well I'm in a generous mood (or kind of disappointed in myself for buying into the hype) and 2 stars is what I'm giving it. My advice (which you probably shouldn't take because everyone else is loving it) is to skip this one entirely. A weak 2 stars.</span>

<div id="review_2065154640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2065154640" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065154640?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784161750" href="/book/show/28352416-the-girl-on-the-train">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=books-to-read-in-romanian">books-to-read-in-romanian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065154640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9068216221167619866">4.45/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/07/04/the-girl-on-the-train-by-paula-hawkins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591475377i/29605232._SY540_.jpg' width='265' height='340' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>
    <b>"I have lost control over everything, even the places in my head."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>I am quite amazed by the fact that this book has been sitting on my bookshelf for like two years already and I haven’t been able to read it until, like, a couple of weeks ago. But then, I remember that I have books older than my brother, sitting and rotting on my bookshelf that have lost all kind of hope in begging me to read them, I just feel better about this</span>
  <span id="freeText9068216221167619866" style="display:none">4.45/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/07/04/the-girl-on-the-train-by-paula-hawkins/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591475377i/29605232._SY540_.jpg" width="265" height="340" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>
    <b>"I have lost control over everything, even the places in my head."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I am quite amazed by the fact that this book has been sitting on my bookshelf for like two years already and I haven’t been able to read it until, like, a couple of weeks ago. But then, I remember that I have books older than my brother, sitting and rotting on my bookshelf that have lost all kind of hope in begging me to read them, I just feel better about this one. <br><br><b>The Girl on the Train</b> by Paula Hawkins is, indeed, a very well-written thriller. At some point in my life, everyone around me talked about this book and now, after reading it, I understand why: it was actually brilliant. <br><br>I cannot say it impressed me at first on the verge of admiration. No. But it was so easy and fast to read that it’s actually made up for my super high expectations (<i>because let’s be honest, you hear so many – SO MANY – things about a hyper hyped book like this and your expectation-o-meter just blows up faster than Chernobyl’s 4th reactor</i>). But, <b>boy</b>. How were the last 100 pages? Oh, don’t ask. I’m still a mess about <b>everything</b> that happened. <br><br>Rachel, our alcoholic, drank much. Like too much and at inappropriate hours. She knows she has a problem. Her life is miserable, it just fell apart, she wants nothing more to do with it and, if you look at it with your eyes closed, it is quite understandable to drown your sorrows in this kind of evil liquids. <br><br>Rachel also has a tendency to distort the reality more than the alcohol in her veins does and keeps imagining all sort of stories for people around her that actually exist, but do not live exactly how she thinks they do. This is the case of her role-model couple, Jason and Jess, aka Scott and Megan (who, in reality, have NOTHING to do with the fake, imaginary couple). This tendency of Rachel’s is maybe another thing that gets her into high trouble because she interchanges her imaginary life with reality. And that can cost her dearly if caught lying. She knows everything, but how much is it true or real? <br><br><i>
  <b>"I'm playing at real life instead of actually living it."</b>
</i><br><br>Further dissecting this novel, a pretty notable aspect is the hidden face of the characters. The three narrative voices of the book have the role of seeing both the exterior and the interior of the characters, which differ ‘from sky to earth’ as we like to say in Romanian (or, an even funnier expression that we use a lot: the exterior of the characters ‘nu se pupă’ with the interior – basically they don’t kiss. Cutie, eh? I know, we are a very lovely breed, us, Romanians, but moving on…). <br><br>Also, the book has the nice particularity of those old and good mystery novels that give you all the details you need to solve the puzzle yourself, but the details are so low-key you don’t even realise they are there (bonus points from me for that concept). Keep the mind open people and you’ll solve the puzzle as I did.<br><br>Before putting an end on this, I would like to discuss another thing that <b>wrecked</b> my nerves. <br><br>Okay, I understood the fact that because of some circumstances, Rachel got an ugly depression and started drinking. But the way she was treated by everyone in her life, including her bastard (ex-)husband is just so cruel and unfair. How is a normal person going to get through tough times when there is no one good by his or her side to push them towards what is right? (<i>more on this topic in the blog post</i>)<br><br>And what I want to further add is that I couldn’t help but notice that there is a certain similarity between Hawkins’ way of putting things in action and Stephen King’s. It is the same cruel manner of expression, with violent truths and obscene language. The same sinister way of presenting reality. The same endless social and moral problems revealed to everyone (for example, the cruel manner of abusing women; that’s just so obvious). It is absolutely fascinating. Oh and yet, another Tom that I absolutely hate from deep within (see: Stephen King’s Tom Rogan in <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/04/24/it-by-stephen-king/" rel="nofollow noopener">It</a>)<br><br>Okay now, with all that being said, I’d like to conclude with the fact that even though this book did not live by the great expectations I’ve created around it, it was actually pretty close. Analysing all those things I encountered during the action, I realised that it is more under the words than above them. And this kind of thing is important because this gives a book the opportunity to live forever.<br><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/774d86be-0904-4e48-9b17-938818440f06_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9068216221167619866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1286269697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286269697" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286269697?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=book-to-film">book-to-film</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286269697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5396180283666476269"><b>”Yesterday---sensible, clearheaded, right-thinking---I decided I must accept that my part in this story was over. But my better angels lost again, defeated by drink, by the person I am when I drink. Drunk Rachel sees no consequences, she is either excessively expansive and optimistic or wrapped up in hate. She has no past, no future. She exists purely in the moment. Drunk Rachel...lies.”</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/S20Stock20Train_zpsafcrgy2r.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537113763i/26311361.jpg' alt=' photo S20Stock20Train_zpsafcrgy2r.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>There are certainly worse ways to spend your day than riding an S stock train into London.</b><br/><br/>Rachel rides the</span>
  <span id="freeText5396180283666476269" style="display:none"><b>”Yesterday---sensible, clearheaded, right-thinking---I decided I must accept that my part in this story was over. But my better angels lost again, defeated by drink, by the person I am when I drink. Drunk Rachel sees no consequences, she is either excessively expansive and optimistic or wrapped up in hate. She has no past, no future. She exists purely in the moment. Drunk Rachel...lies.”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/S20Stock20Train_zpsafcrgy2r.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537113763i/26311361.jpg" alt=" photo S20Stock20Train_zpsafcrgy2r.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>There are certainly worse ways to spend your day than riding an S stock train into London.</b><br><br>Rachel rides the train into London every day to keep up the pretense that she has a job. The truth is she lost her job months ago when she showed up to work inebriated, not just buzzed or mildly intoxicated, but sloppy drunk. She can’t exactly put her finger on when she first started to drink too much. It was around the time when she was trying to get pregnant with her now ex-husband Tom. <br><br>He impregnated his mistress instead. <br><br><b>”The dagger in my heart twists, round and round and round.”</b><br><br>Anna, slender little Anna, is now living in her house with her husband with a child that should have been hers. Rachel used to be attractive, curvy, and pretty, but now the curves have lost their buoyancy, and her face has become puffy. She is melting down into someone unrecognizable. The pain that used to be internalized is now manifesting itself into a grotesque mask. She drinks to escape. <i>”When I drink, I hardly sleep at all. I pass out cold for an hour or two, then I wake, sick with fear, sick with myself. If I have a day when I don’t drink, that night I fall into the heaviest of slumbers, a deep unconsciousness, and in the morning I cannot wake properly, I cannot shake sleep, it stays with me for hours, sometimes for days.”</i> Drinking doesn’t work, not drinking is worse. <br><br><b>Sometimes she blacks out.</b> <br><br>The problem with <b>THAT</b> is she loses so much control over what she does or what she remembers. When she blacks out she has to believe what others tell her. This is when she writes painfully embarrassing emails to her ex-husband. This is when she is capable of doing something that she would never consider doing sober. <br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Girl20on20the20Train_zpsoyghwdb4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537113764i/26311362.jpg" alt=" photo Girl20on20the20Train_zpsoyghwdb4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The train takes Rachel by her old life every day. The subdivision with the beautiful house that she thought would be hers forever is part of her daily view. She can look right into the backyards of the homes, and there she starts to notice a couple, a perfect couple who seem to love each other. She projects a life onto them, even giving them names, and starts to look forward to any glimpse of them that will allow her to add to the fairy tale narrative that she has been assembling about them on her daily rides into work. Then one day she sees something that brings the whole house of cards tumbling down. <br><br>We can look at other people and think their lives are wonderful. They must be leading so much more successful and meaningful lives than we do. The problem of course is that we know everything about our lives. Every failure is duly noted on a spooling list. Our successes are tempered by our own feelings of inadequacies. Every debilitating slight to our self-esteem etches away at the foundation of our ability to see beyond the things that have went wrong. What we have to remind ourselves of is that, though people may seem to be leading perfect lives, everybody has problems. Don’t fool yourself, and don’t let them fool you either. We are all doomed to be disappointed, to falter, to make mistakes, and sometimes destroy ourselves. Scott and Megan, as it turns out, are no different. Her mythical couple have names as it turns out, not the ones she chose for them. <br><br><b>When Megan disappears Rachel realizes that she saw something. <br><br>The problem is she is an irresponsible drunk.</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Rear20Window_zpsjn2vd2qs.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537113764i/26311363.jpg" alt=" photo Rear20Window_zpsjn2vd2qs.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book is certainly an ode to one of my favorite films <i>Rear Window</i>. (For those youngsters out there, you might be more familiar with the film <i>Disturbia</i>.) Jimmy Stewart is incapacitated with a broken leg, but Rachel may actually be more incapacitated by her drinking. Rachel is the definition of an unreliable narrator. I didn’t what to believe her, not necessarily because I felt she was lying, but because she was so wasted most of the time that even her version of sober might be my version of being buzzed. The characters in this book are not very endearing. As we learn more about them we find less and less to like about them. Be warned about these characters if you are a reader that must like the people you read about. <br><br>The plot certainly reminded me of an Agatha Christie. I often found myself munching down on a red herring served on a Ritz Cracker and washed down with a decent Merlot. I didn’t enjoy this book as much as I did the modern noir novels of <i>Peter Swanson</i>, but I don’t think I’m going to be forgetting this book any time soon. If that proves to be the case, I might even need to bump it one star. <br><br>There is talk of Emily Blunt starring in the upcoming movie which could lend the project some extra attention. This book, with this plot, should translate well to screen. Don’t feel guilty if you decide to wait for the movie. Paula Hawkins has laid out a script that shouldn’t need much tucking or trimming for the big screen. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5396180283666476269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4352695106914552874">this. book. suuuuuuuucks.<br/><br/>i can't believe it was an international sensation. i can't believe it was adapted into a movie <s>starring actual queen emily blunt</s>. i can't believe it SOLD A SINGLE COPY. (i didn't buy this one. my mom did. so there.)<br/><br/>this is just...a straight up bad book on every level. the characters are so insanely unlikable it's cartoonish. it'd be funny if it didn't make EVERY SECOND OF THIS BOOK, EVERY PAGE, EVERY WORD, A FRESH HELL TO FIGHT THROUGH IN ORDER TO GET TO THE NEXT ONE, WH</span>
  <span id="freeText4352695106914552874" style="display:none">this. book. suuuuuuuucks.<br /><br />i can't believe it was an international sensation. i can't believe it was adapted into a movie <s>starring actual queen emily blunt</s>. i can't believe it SOLD A SINGLE COPY. (i didn't buy this one. my mom did. so there.)<br /><br />this is just...a straight up bad book on every level. the characters are so insanely unlikable it's cartoonish. it'd be funny if it didn't make EVERY SECOND OF THIS BOOK, EVERY PAGE, EVERY WORD, A FRESH HELL TO FIGHT THROUGH IN ORDER TO GET TO THE NEXT ONE, WHICH IS, GUESS WHAT, ALSO HELL.<br /><br />this would be maybe O.K. or at least survivable if this book was scary or thrilling or spooky or intriguing at all, but guess what, IT ISN'T. just some lady getting blasted on vodka and riding a train. looking out some windows. sometimes sneaking a peek at a house. <br /><br />the entertainment potential is almost overwhelming.<br /><br />honestly all i really want from a thriller = some thrills. that really does not seem like too much to ask for, considering IT'S THE F*CKING NAME OF THE WHOLE ENTIRE GENRE. and the reveal of this makes it even worse.<br /><br />bottom line: straight up one of the worst books i've ever read. are there people who like this book? if so, HOW????<br /><br />(this is part of a project i'm doing where i write mini-reviews of books i read a long time ago. this parenthetical insert is a constant snoozefest)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4352695106914552874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14352203863475374764">Half a "what the hell happened ?" star !!<br/><br/><b> 2016 Worst Read of the Year </b><br/><br/>Original Review written October 3, 2016<br/><br/>Update : October 25, 2016 (mini review of the film !!)<br/><br/>A couple of days ago 4 single girls (well women in their forties and fifties), my bf (convinced him to join us and he agreed if I took him to Denny's afterwards) and myself went to see this film. This is the main reason I read the book as we had planned this outing for months and then I read the book just before the film came out.<br/><br/>As yo</span>
  <span id="freeText14352203863475374764" style="display:none">Half a "what the hell happened ?" star !!<br /><br /><b> 2016 Worst Read of the Year </b><br /><br />Original Review written October 3, 2016<br /><br />Update : October 25, 2016 (mini review of the film !!)<br /><br />A couple of days ago 4 single girls (well women in their forties and fifties), my bf (convinced him to join us and he agreed if I took him to Denny's afterwards) and myself went to see this film. This is the main reason I read the book as we had planned this outing for months and then I read the book just before the film came out.<br /><br />As you prolly already know I abhored the book so I was grotesquely curious about the film.<br /><br />First though I want to give the rating of my lovely galpals when I polled them afterwards over omelettes !!<br /><br />Gal One : Book 4 stars Film 3.5 stars<br />Gal Two: Book 4 stars Film 3 stars<br />Gal Three: Book 3 stars Film 4 stars<br />Gal Four: Book 3 stars Film 3 stars<br /><br />BF - refused to read the book Film 3 stars<br /><br />Jaidee Book 0.5 star Film 1.5 stars (in comparison Gone Girl Book 2.5 stars Film 3 stars)<br /><br />The film was seriously lacking, terrible dialogue, fairly poor acting (with a few exceptions), mostly very dull when it was not ridiculous.<br /><br />What I liked - Emily Blunt gave a 3 star decent performance<br /> There was some really cool art and some beautiful brief cinematography<br /><br />Saving Grace: Officer Riley played by Allison Janney was awesome. She had the right amount of wit and chutzpah for the role. She shone in her brief moments. Plus I love the way she is aging...so beautiful in a natural and haggard way.<br /><br />Am I glad I saw it ? Yes...time with my good friends and holding hands with my BF is always nice.<br /><br />Am I glad I read the book? Hell No!!<br /> <br /><br /><br /><br />Original review September 26, 2016:<br /><br />This book makes Gone Girl look like a masterpiece !!!<br /><br /> At six percent I was very pleasantly surprised.<br /> At eighty-seven percent I wanted to tear my hair out on the ludicrousness and ridiculousness of this book.<br /><br /><br /> Recipe for this disaster<br /><br /> - you start with three of the most unlikable women (ever...i mean ever) and you stir slowly<br /> ( one is a pathetic alcoholic, the other is narcissistic and the third is troubled) until they are mixed so thoroughly that you can't tell them apart except that you hate them all<br /> <br /> -you start with an excellent premise that goes nowhere and so you have all three women terribly dependent on the men in their lives except they all cheat on the men in their lives and they all hate each other which makes you hate them even more<br /><br />-oh all the women are liars, cheats and oh so bored with their pampered lives....oh lets blame this on trauma, hardships , grief....ya we can be assholes becuz we hurt so bad.....now not only do you hate them...you want to bitch slap them too....but oh no you cant do that because they do it to each other and plan each other's physical and psychological demise .....<br /><br />-just when you think it can't get any worse...yes you got it...let's blame it on a man....oh yes he is a sociopath and yes all three women love him...boo hoo hoo <br /><br />-do we know what motivates these women (of course we don't) just suspend your disbelief so far that you think you might be on Pluto !!!<br /><br />Sorry for the rant but this book is a bloody train wreck and how it won the awards and accolades it has is beyond me.<br /><br />I apologize Ms. Flynn...you don't seem nearly so bad any more.<br /><br />Not only should I not have not gotten on this stupid train but I should have ran away instead.<br /><br />Addendum: Here is a funny little Youtube compilation where my review has a little cameo role :D<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kO7l_LMJWw8">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kO7l_...</a><br /><br /><br />Bloody Awful :(</span>

<div id="review_1377742036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377742036" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1377742036?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=literature">literature</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1377742036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9015562957760381709">The Girl on the Train, Paula Hawkins<br/><br/>The Girl on the Train (2015) is a psychological thriller novel by British author Paula Hawkins. <br/><br/>The story is a first-person narrative told from the point of view of three women: Rachel, Anna, and Megan. <br/><br/>Rachel Watson is a 33-year-old alcoholic, reeling from the end of her marriage to Tom, who left her for another woman, Anna Boyd. Rachel's drinking has caused her to lose her job; she frequently binges and has blackouts. <br/><br/>While drunk, she often harasses Tom, tho</span>
  <span id="freeText9015562957760381709" style="display:none">The Girl on the Train, Paula Hawkins<br /><br />The Girl on the Train (2015) is a psychological thriller novel by British author Paula Hawkins. <br /><br />The story is a first-person narrative told from the point of view of three women: Rachel, Anna, and Megan. <br /><br />Rachel Watson is a 33-year-old alcoholic, reeling from the end of her marriage to Tom, who left her for another woman, Anna Boyd. Rachel's drinking has caused her to lose her job; she frequently binges and has blackouts. <br /><br />While drunk, she often harasses Tom, though she has little or no memory of these acts once she sobers up. Tom is now married to Anna and has a daughter with her, Evie – a situation that fuels Rachel's self-destructive tendencies, as it was her inability to conceive a child that began her spiral into alcoholism. <br /><br />Rachel follows her old routine of taking the train to London every day; her train slowly passes her old house, where Tom, Anna, and Evie now live. She also begins watching from the train an attractive couple who live a few houses away from Tom. She idealists their life (christening them "Jason" and "Jess"), though she has no idea that their life is far from perfect. <br /><br />The wife of the couple, Megan Hipwell ("Jess"), has a troubled past. She finds her life boring, and escapes from her troubles by taking a series of lovers. Megan has sought help by seeing a therapist, Dr. Kamal Abdic. Eventually, she reveals to him a dark secret she has never confided to anyone before.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه ژوئن سال 2015میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: دختری در قطار؛ پائولا هاوکینز؛ مترجم: محبوبه موسوی؛ تهران، میلکان، 1393، در 385ص، شابک 9786007845008؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: دختری در قطار؛ پائولا هاوکینز؛ مترجم: علی قانع؛ تهران، آموت، 1394، در 352ص، شابک 9786003840140؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، کوله پشتی، 1395، در 343ص؛ شابک 9786008211051؛<br /><br />عنوان: دختری در قطار؛ پائولا هاوکینز؛ مترجم: جواد رحمتی فرد؛ تهران، نگارش الکترونیک کتاب، 1394، در 400ص؛ <br /><br />عنوان: دختری در قطار؛ پائولا هاوکینز؛ مترجم: فرانک سالاری؛ تهران، البرز، 1394، در 384ص؛ <br /><br />عنوان: دختری در قطار؛ پائولا هاوکینز؛ مترجم: مهرآئین اخوت؛ تهران، هیرمند، 1394، در 412ص؛ شابک 9789644083891؛<br /><br />دختری در قطار؛ پلیسی، و تریلری روان‌ شناسانه، است، داستان توسط راوی اول شخص و از زاویه ی دید سه زن: «ریچل»، «آنا» و «مگان» بازگو می‌شود.؛ گویا کتاب موفق شده، رکورد پرفروش‌ترین‌ها همچون «هری پاتر» را نیز بشکند، و هم‌چنان در صدر باقی بماند؛ برخی این رمان را، جلد دوم «دختر گمشده»، می‌دانند.؛ ماجرای همیشگی عشق و شکست، اینبار با همراهی افکاری سرگردان، به داستانی معمایی، منجر شده، دختری در قطار با روایتی مدرن، سراغ موضوعی کلاسیک رفته است.؛ «ریچل» که زنی دائم‌ الخمر است، برای خودش ارزشی قائل نیست، از نظر او، زنان، تنها از دو وجه، قابل توجه‌ اند «وضعیت ظاهری»، و «نقش مادری»‌ ایشان.؛ و ...؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 05/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
