<div id="review_1166073081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166073081" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166073081?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166073081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9600924838228811717"><b>
  <u>All aboard!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>TRUST NO ONE</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>I have lost control over everything, even the places in my head.</i>
</b><br/><br/>What? “Trust No One”? Why is that sign on the railroad of this review? Is this a “The X-Files” story? Oh, no, but certainly the motto of that iconic TV series is a good advice to anyone who dares to aboard this train of thought in this very particular journey to the minds of three women that you may think that they are quite different, but...<br/><br/>...maybe not...<br/><br/>...or maybe they do...<br/><br/>...mmh...<br/><br/>...rememb</span>
  <span id="freeText9600924838228811717" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>All aboard!!!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>TRUST NO ONE</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>I have lost control over everything, even the places in my head.</i>
</b><br /><br />What? “Trust No One”? Why is that sign on the railroad of this review? Is this a “The X-Files” story? Oh, no, but certainly the motto of that iconic TV series is a good advice to anyone who dares to aboard this train of thought in this very particular journey to the minds of three women that you may think that they are quite different, but...<br /><br />...maybe not...<br /><br />...or maybe they do...<br /><br />...mmh...<br /><br />...remember about trust no one?...<br /><br />...we’ll even you should not trust me neither...<br /><br />...bwa-ha-ha-ha-ha!!!<br /><br />No, I’m kidding! I’m your friendly reviewer, surely you can <i>trust me</i>...<br /><br />...bwa-ha-ha-ha!!!<br /><br />Okay, enough misleading malevolent mirth... for the moment...<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BROKEN DOLLS</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>There’s nothing so painful, so corrosive as suspicion.</i>
</b><br /><br />In this story you will have three voices in your head...<br /><br /><u>Rachel:</u> An alcoholic woman who failed in marriage.<br /><br /><u>Megan:</u> A pretentious woman who succeed in cheating.<br /><br /><u>Anna:</u> A married woman who who succeed in pretention.<br /><br />All of them are unlikely protagonists, hardly role models, sinners paying for their own faults, broken dolls in the middle of a railroad where fate is the train.<br /><br />They did their mistakes, but your own mistake can be to trust them... or me...<br /><br />...bwa-ha-ha-ha!!!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>WHAT WORKED BEFORE, WILL WORK AGAIN</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>There’s something comforting about the sight of strangers safe at home.</i>
</b><br /><br />You may heard that this story is the “new” <i>Gone Girl</i>, and you would have heard well then.<br /><br />Actually, while it’s understandable that everybody knows about <i>Gone Girl</i>, there is another newer book that it could considered too into the formula in a sense...<br /><br /><i>Gone Girl</i> meets <i>Elizabeth is Missing</i><br /><br />And also, there are two movies that came to my mind, no wonder, from the master of suspense, Alfred Hitchcock (who I have no doubt that if he would be still alive, he would adapt into a film this novel)...<br /><br /><i>Rear Window</i> meets <i>The Lady Vanishes</i><br /><br />That, yes, they were based on previously printed material too.<br /><br />So, if you are fair familiarized with all those mentioned stories, you can quite well expect lots of trains, losses of memory, missing women, vouyerisms and misleadings...<br /><br />Bwa-ha-ha-ha!!!... wait! Why did I laughed this time? I believe that it’s one of the moments where you can trust me more... or isn’t?<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>EVERYTHING IS ACCORDING TO THE PLAN</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Life is not a paragraph, and death is no parenthesis.</i>
</b><br /><br />You may notice or not, while reading the different railroads, that the debutant, Paula Hawkins, the author, didn’t put anything random on the book, everything is according to the plan, even the dates, that honestly, they aren’t easy to keep on mind, but even those dates denote different kind of railway engines, while a side of the story can be told as a paused steam locomotive, another side is indeed a bullet train.<br /><br />But in any case, life hardly can be told in an instant, even the fastest deposition needs time, life is rich, life is complex, and if there is a saying that “each man is a world”, well I can say that each woman is an universe, a wonderful universe full of surprises, and while maybe in a whole another kind of context but (death) is hardly an ending, but just other twist in life.<br /><br />And what could be life without those wonderful unexpected twists?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9600924838228811717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1188482323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1188482323" />
    <a title="Joanne Harris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34428697-joanne-harris"><img alt="Joanne Harris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442439458p2/34428697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1188482323?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne Harris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne Harris" href="/user/show/34428697-joanne-harris">Joanne Harris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1188482323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5962102890463548876">This was a perfectly decent, well-crafted thriller, which I happened not to like very much, for reasons that have little to do with its craft or its quality. This sometimes happens, and it doesn't mean that others won't enjoy it. The plot is fast-moving and with some real surprises. The portrayal of alcoholism is great (although I would have liked it to go further into the more visceral details, rather than skimming the surface of the theme). <br/>However (and yes, I know it's trivial, but) the title</span>
  <span id="freeText5962102890463548876" style="display:none">This was a perfectly decent, well-crafted thriller, which I happened not to like very much, for reasons that have little to do with its craft or its quality. This sometimes happens, and it doesn't mean that others won't enjoy it. The plot is fast-moving and with some real surprises. The portrayal of alcoholism is great (although I would have liked it to go further into the more visceral details, rather than skimming the surface of the theme). <br />However (and yes, I know it's trivial, but) the title. I'm getting tired of these vaguely infantilizing titles that refer to mature women as "girls" (although, to be honest, none of the female characters seemed at all mature to me). The multiple-person narration was nicely-handled, except that all three narrators sounded the same, to the extent of noticing the same things and recording them in the exact same register and vocabulary. And although I have no problem enjoying books with unsympathetic characters, I found the women in this book not only unsympathetic, but really rather dull, relying on the "damaged woman" trope for interest, rather than investing the characters with anything more tangible. The publishers are pushing this book as a second GONE GIRL. I was hoping for something new. Not this time, I'm afraid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5962102890463548876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1764167364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764167364" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764167364?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764167364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12761841890199354609">This book was INTOXICATING. I loved every single second of it. While I had gone into this story thinking it was going to be packed with suspenseful scenes, the mystery was really in the storytelling. It was unexpected but executed SOOOO well. A+ use of an unreliable narrator that propelled the story way beyond what I had originally anticipated. Not only was it extremely thrilling and kept me intrigued the entire time, but I seriously appreciated how accurate the representation of alcoholism was.</span>
  <span id="freeText12761841890199354609" style="display:none">This book was INTOXICATING. I loved every single second of it. While I had gone into this story thinking it was going to be packed with suspenseful scenes, the mystery was really in the storytelling. It was unexpected but executed SOOOO well. A+ use of an unreliable narrator that propelled the story way beyond what I had originally anticipated. Not only was it extremely thrilling and kept me intrigued the entire time, but I seriously appreciated how accurate the representation of alcoholism was. While the events of the story were not necessarily the most "realistic", the many of the characters felt real; like people who could actually exist, who had authentic thoughts and feelings I could see reflected in actual people. It was a fantastic novel and I would highly highly recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12761841890199354609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1850754114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850754114" />
    <a title="Federico DN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn"><img alt="Federico DN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478986000p2/29005117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1850754114?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Federico DN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Federico DN" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn">Federico DN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29005117-federico-dn?shelf=almost-fav">almost-fav</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850754114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14335449133776991314">Sometimes people aren't bad, sometimes they just simply make an infinity of bad decisions.<br/><br/>In this novel we learn the story of Rachel Watson, a young englishwoman, divorced and part time alcoholic. Everyday she travels by train, enjoying its harmonic pace, its unhurried sounds and the everyday regular people that she already feels she knows, but, above everything, she loves to watch the house number fifteen on Blenheim street, where lives her imaginary perfect couple, Jess and Jason.<br/><br/>Until one day</span>
  <span id="freeText14335449133776991314" style="display:none">Sometimes people aren't bad, sometimes they just simply make an infinity of bad decisions.<br /><br />In this novel we learn the story of Rachel Watson, a young englishwoman, divorced and part time alcoholic. Everyday she travels by train, enjoying its harmonic pace, its unhurried sounds and the everyday regular people that she already feels she knows, but, above everything, she loves to watch the house number fifteen on Blenheim street, where lives her imaginary perfect couple, Jess and Jason.<br /><br />Until one day her dreamy beautiful couple, for reasons we are not going to spoil, ceases to be. Something happens and nothing will ever be the same. Something happens and her already problematic life will change forever; her future, and the past she once thought she knew.<br /><br />Starts somewhat slow but in short time becomes very gripping, and as the story progresses, it becomes even grippier still, maintaining that spectacular atmosphere from beginning to end. A certified good thriller. Hardly difficult to disappoint.<br /><br />**** The movie is a faithful adaptation of the book. Emily Blunt delivers a remarkable performance, really worthy of recognition. However, due to several shortcomings, the movie is quite far to being as gripping or captivating as the book. A bad guy you can see coming from the very beginning, and several important omissions. Still, interestingly enough to complement the reading.<br /><br />Until next time,<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />A veces la gente no es mala, a veces sólo simplemente toma una infinidad de malas decisiones.<br /><br />En esta novela conocemos la historia de Rachel Watson, una joven inglesa, divorciada y alcohólica part time. Todos los días viaja en tren, disfrutando de su armónico andar, su parsimonioso sonido y la gente habitué que de tanto ver ya cree conocer; pero, por sobre todas las cosas, ama ver la casa número quince de la calle Blenheim, donde habita su imaginada pareja perfecta, Jess y Jason.<br /><br />Hasta que un día su soñada maravillosa pareja, por razones que no queremos spoilear, deja de serlo. Algo sucede y nada volverá a ser igual. Algo sucede y su ya problemática vida cambiará para siempre, tanto su futuro, como el pasado que una vez creía conocer.<br /><br />Empieza algo lento pero en poco tiempo se vuelve muy atrapante, y mientras más avanza más cautivante aún, manteniendo ese espectacular clima desde el principio hasta el final. Un buen thriller asegurado. Recomendable. Dificilmente capaz de decepcionar. <br /><br />**** La película es una adaptación fiel a la obra. Emily Blunt hace un papel destacado, realmente digno de reconocimiento. Sin embargo, por algunas falencias la película está bastante lejos de ser tan atrapante y cautivante como el libro. Un malo que se ve llegar desde el principio y ciertas omisiones importantes. Aunque igualmente lo suficientemente interesante como para complementar la lectura.<br /><br />Hasta la próxima,</span>
  <a data-text-id="14335449133776991314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I can imagine the latter being a sensation upon publishing.<br /><br />Rachel is the girl on the train. She is the key to everything that happens in the book, but she's an unreliable witness. It's not life, it's fiction at its best.</span>

<div id="review_1216775278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216775278" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216775278?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=addiction">addiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=crime-and-or-madness">crime-and-or-madness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=couple-love-and-hate">couple-love-and-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=quirky">quirky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=debuts">debuts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216775278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13238139660367500172">Seems like this train took everyone to Gushland, but I got waylaid in Mediocre-ville. Comparing this book to Hitchcock is just laughable. Okay, okay, it does start out with intrigue, as the girl, Rachel, sits on the train day after day, and obsessively peeks at a house where she can see a man and a woman moving around. She gives them names and imagines a perfect life and perfect marriage for them. This voyeurism is pretty cool. A great beginning.<br/> <br/>But I wish Rachel had stayed on the train. In fac</span>
  <span id="freeText13238139660367500172" style="display:none">Seems like this train took everyone to Gushland, but I got waylaid in Mediocre-ville. Comparing this book to Hitchcock is just laughable. Okay, okay, it does start out with intrigue, as the girl, Rachel, sits on the train day after day, and obsessively peeks at a house where she can see a man and a woman moving around. She gives them names and imagines a perfect life and perfect marriage for them. This voyeurism is pretty cool. A great beginning.<br /> <br />But I wish Rachel had stayed on the train. In fact, I wish the train had been the setting for the whole book and that the plot had turned into something twisty about mysterious commuters. Instead (and in my mind, tragically), Rachel gets off the train. And then the story is all about Rachel getting drunk, Rachel calling her ex while drunk, Rachel trying to remember things that happened while drunk, Rachel pissing off her roommate while drunk, and Rachel being ashamed about being drunk. And around and around. Yes, this gets really boring. We spend a lot of time inside Rachel’s head, and though this works in many books, it’s tedious here.<br /> <br />I will say that despite this, the first-person voice drew me in. Most of the book is Rachel’s voice, though two other women sometimes tell their stories. All three voices are articulate and make you feel all chummy with the narrator. The language has a good flow to it, and the book is easy to read and has a really nice tone. <br /><br />On the flip side, all three women speak in the exact same way; their voices are interchangeable. This makes them seem less like real characters; I become aware that there is just one person and that’s the author. Not being able to create different personalities with their own voices is a common weakness in authors, especially new ones, but that doesn’t make it less annoying. It seems amateurish.<br /> <br />The plot is about a woman who goes missing. Rachel the drunken mess is a busybody who sticks her nose in and tries to find out what happened. The cast of characters includes her ex, his new wife, a therapist, and the fantasy couple Rachel saw from the train. The characters are well drawn but their behaviors don’t tell us enough to let us figure out whodunit. There just aren’t enough clues, which is always a letdown. I want to guess, and I want to have a chance of getting it right. The mystery is suddenly solved at the very end--all the suspense is saved up for those final 70 or so pages. The reveal is satisfying, and for me is a surprise, but the read is definitely uneven. The final scenes are well-written and action-packed, but the majority of the book is sort of slow and repetitive.<br /> <br />Oh, and not only was the book not like Hitchcock, it most definitely was not like Gone Girl, a truly spectacular psychological thriller. Once again, I’m left thinking, huh? Are you kidding me? How come I missed the train to Gushland? Rachel should have stayed on the damn train and I might have ended up in the same town as everyone else. Instead, as I said, Mediocre-ville for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13238139660367500172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1363876995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1363876995?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1363876995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4260364568686371826">in all honesty, i only read this because i felt like i could not stop seeing this everywhere. so. many. people. were reading this. on the tube, in the park, at the bookshop. i couldnt escape seeing this book.<br/><br/>and after all the hype it got (which was an impossibly surprising amount for only a debut novel), i honestly was very let down. i couldnt stand rachel (or any other character, actually) and therefore, i found myself not invested in the story. i finished it just because i needed to know ‘whod</span>
  <span id="freeText4260364568686371826" style="display:none">in all honesty, i only read this because i felt like i could not stop seeing this everywhere. so. many. people. were reading this. on the tube, in the park, at the bookshop. i couldnt escape seeing this book.<br /><br />and after all the hype it got (which was an impossibly surprising amount for only a debut novel), i honestly was very let down. i couldnt stand rachel (or any other character, actually) and therefore, i found myself not invested in the story. i finished it just because i needed to know ‘whodunnit.’ i will admit, i can see the appeal and understand why this became so popular. but for me, i just wasnt into it. <br /><br />guess i will be a little more careful about giving in to peer pressure next time an overly hyped book comes around. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2.5 stars</i></b></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1eWc+uYIZLs43pMT1quyo9o5lkD5vKwIkLkzdQmV+p/vw/UoXVat05/1J3IhXrh8DGZxiDcxIm/Lx3XExNYIBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q0KDPZobbwjbz0/aFSpElCwkBX8TqtKMdlbjKrkOz3x5ZOrvIUWmYHzk+7vi305L+nvit90nXOstKKWbdE095g==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_19288043'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043-gone-girl?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Gone Girl<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Gillian Flynn<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.08 avg rating &mdash; 2,344,340 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2012\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer8358414523799412549\">Marriage can be a real killer.\n\nOn a warm summer morning in North Carthage, Missouri, it is Nick and Amy Dunne’s fifth wedding anniversary. Presents are being wrapped and reservations are being made when Nick’s clever and beautiful wife disappears fr<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8358414523799412549\" style=\"display:none\">Marriage can be a real killer.\n\nOn a warm summer morning in North Carthage, Missouri, it is Nick and Amy Dunne’s fifth wedding anniversary. Presents are being wrapped and reservations are being made when Nick’s clever and beautiful wife disappears from their rented McMansion on the Mississippi River. Husband-of-the-Year Nick isn’t doing himself any favors with cringe-worthy daydreams about the slope and shape of his wife’s head, but passages from Amy\'s diary reveal the alpha-girl perfectionist could have put anyone dangerously on edge. Under mounting pressure from the police and the media—as well as Amy’s fiercely doting parents—the town golden boy parades an endless series of lies, deceits, and inappropriate behavior. Nick is oddly evasive, and he’s definitely bitter—but is he really a killer?\n\nAs the cops close in, every couple in town is soon wondering how well they know the one that they love. With his twin sister, Margo, at his side, Nick stands by his innocence. Trouble is, if Nick didn’t do it, where is that beautiful wife? And what was in that silvery gift box hidden in the back of her bedroom closet?\n\nWith her razor-sharp writing and trademark psychological insight, Gillian Flynn delivers a fast-paced, devilishly dark, and ingeniously plotted thriller that confirms her status as one of the hottest writers around.\n\nOne of the most critically acclaimed suspense writers of our time, New York Times bestseller Gillian Flynn takes that statement to its darkest place in this unputdownable masterpiece about a marriage gone terribly, terribly wrong. The Chicago Tribune proclaimed that her work “draws you in and keeps you reading with the force of a pure but nasty addiction.” Gone Girl’s toxic mix of sharp-edged wit and deliciously chilling prose
